window['google_ads']
=
google_ads;




if(google_ads.length
!=
0)
{








apply_ad_config(google_ads.length);









render_ads(true,
window['ad_config_top']);









if(window['backfillParam'])
{












window['backfillParam']['pl_rnum']
=
google_ads.length;












window['backfillParam']['pl_time']
=
Date.now()
-
afc_ad_start_time;








}




}
}

function
apply_ad_config(num)
{
window['ad_config_top']
=
Math.min(2,
num);
window['ad_config_bot']
=
Math.min(2,
num);
}

google_ad_client
=
'ca-aj-cat';
google_ad_channel
=
'cx_ask_wiki,ad_dirN';
google_ad_output
=
'js';
google_max_num_ads
=
'4';
google_ad_type
=
'text';
google_image_size
=
'';
google_num_ads_recieved=
'';
google_language
=
'';
google_country
=
'';
google_encoding
=
'utf8';
google_safe
=
'medium';
google_adtest
=
'off';
google_ad_section
=
'default';
google_page_url
=
'';
google_hints
=
'Garth_Brooks';
google_kw
=
'';
google_kw_type
=
'broad';


var
backfillParam
=
{




pl_rqnum
:
google_max_num_ads,




pl_hints
:
google_hints,




pl_rp
:
"false",




pl_kw
:
google_kw,




pl_cl
:
google_ad_client,




pl_ch
:
google_ad_channel,




pl_hex
:
"#FDFEEE",




pl_type
:
"afc",




pl_clksp
:
"none"};

var
word_arr
;

var
word_arr_len
;


function
highlightQuery(input_str)
{

var
queryTokenArray
=
"brooks,garth,_,";


var
tok_arr
=
queryTokenArray.split(",");

for(tok_arr_idx=0;
tok_arr_idx
<
tok_arr.length-1;
tok_arr_idx
++)
{

if(isCombinationWord(tok_arr[tok_arr_idx])){
word_arr
=
tok_arr[tok_arr_idx].split("-");
word_arr_len
=
word_arr.length;
first_pos
=
input_str.toLowerCase().indexOf(word_arr[0],0);

if(first_pos
!=-1)
{
input_str
=
highlightCombinationWords(input_str,first_pos);
}
}
else
{
first_pos
=
input_str.toLowerCase().indexOf(tok_arr[tok_arr_idx],0);
if(first_pos
!=
-1
&&
tok_arr[tok_arr_idx].length
>
0)
{
input_str
=
highlightSimpleWords(input_str,tok_arr[tok_arr_idx],first_pos);
}
}
}
return
input_str;
}

function
isCombinationWord(word){
if(word.indexOf("-")
!=
-1){
return
true;
}
else
{
return
false;
}
}


function
isAlpha(ch)
{
if
(ch
!=
null
&&
ch.match(/^[a-zA-Z0-9]+$/)){
return
true;
}
return
false;
}

function
isQueryinInput(firstindex,
input_str,
j){
for(i=firstindex;
i<
input_str.length
;
++i)
{
var
currindex
=
i;

if(!isAlpha(input_str.charAt(i)))
{
if(firstindex
==
currindex)

{
firstindex++;
}
else
{
if(word_arr[j]
!=
input_str.substring(firstindex,currindex).toLowerCase())
return
-1;
if
(j
==
word_arr_len-1)
return
currindex;
else
return
isQueryinInput(currindex+1,input_str,++j);
}
}
}

if(j
<
word_arr_len)
{
if(word_arr[j]
!=
input_str.substring(firstindex,currindex+1).toLowerCase())
return
-1;
}

return
(currindex
+
1)
;
}


function

highlightCombinationWords(input_str,first_pos)
{
exactmatch
=
isQueryinInput(first_pos+word_arr[0].length,input_str,1)
;
if(exactmatch
!=-1
)

{
bold_str
=
"<b>"
+
input_str.substring(first_pos,exactmatch)
+
"</b>";
input_str
=
input_str.substring(0,first_pos)
+
bold_str
+
input_str.substring(exactmatch);
next_pos
=
input_str.toLowerCase().indexOf(word_arr[0],exactmatch+7);
while(next_pos
!=
-1)
{
return
highlightCombinationWords(input_str,next_pos);
}
}
return
input_str;
}


function

highlightSimpleWords(input_str,token,
first_pos)
{
var
end_pos
=
first_pos
+
token.length;
if(!isAlpha(input_str.charAt(end_pos))
&&
!isAlpha(input_str.charAt(first_pos-1))){
bold_str
=
"<b>"
+
input_str.substring(first_pos,end_pos)
+
"</b>";
input_str
=
input_str.substring(0,first_pos)
+
bold_str
+
input_str.substring(end_pos);
next_pos
=
input_str.toLowerCase().indexOf(token,end_pos+7);
}
else
{
next_pos
=
input_str.toLowerCase().indexOf(token,end_pos);
}

while(next_pos
!=
-1)
{
return
highlightSimpleWords(input_str,token,next_pos);
}
return
input_str;
}</script>

<p><b>Troyal
Garth
Brooks</b>
(born
February
7,
1962)
is
an
American
<a
href="/wiki/Country_music?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Country
music">country
music</a>
singer
and
songwriter.
His
eponymous
first
album
was
released
in
1989
and
peaked
at
Number
2
in
the
US
country
album
chart
while
climbing
to
number
13
on
the
Billboard
200
album
chart.
Brooks'
integration
of
rock
elements
into
his
recordings
and
live
performances
earned
him
immense
popularity.
This
progressive
approach
allowed
him
to
dominate
the
country
single
and
album
charts
while
crossing
over
into
the
mainstream
pop
arena.<sup
id="cite_ref-johnsonag_1-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-johnsonag-1"><span>[</span>1<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>Brooks
broke
records
for
both
sales
and
concert
attendance
throughout
the
1990s.
As
of
2013,
his
recordings
continue
to
sell
well
and,
according
to
Nielsen
Soundscan,
his
albums
sales
up
to
May
2013
are
68,630,000,<sup
id="cite_ref-2"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-2"><span>[</span>2<span>]</span></a></sup>
which
makes
him
the
<a
href="/wiki/List_of_best-selling_music_artists_in_the_United_States?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="List
of
best-selling
music
artists
in
the
United
States">best-selling
albums
artist
in
the
United
States
in
the
SoundScan
era</a>
(since
1991),
a
title
held
since
1991,
well
over
5
million
ahead
of
his
nearest
rival,
<a
href="/wiki/The_Beatles?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="The
Beatles">The
Beatles</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-3"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-3"><span>[</span>3<span>]</span></a></sup>
According
to
<a
href="/wiki/RIAA?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="RIAA"
class="mw-redirect">RIAA</a>
he
is
the
<a
href="/wiki/List_of_best-selling_music_artists_in_the_United_States?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="List
of
best-selling
music
artists
in
the
United
States">second
best-selling
solo
albums
artist
in
the
United
States
of
all
time</a>
behind
<a
href="/wiki/Elvis_Presley?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Elvis
Presley">Elvis
Presley</a>
(overall
third
to
the
Beatles
and
Elvis
Presley)
with
128
million
units
sold.<sup
id="cite_ref-4"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-4"><span>[</span>4<span>]</span></a></sup>
Brooks
is
also
one
of
the
<a
href="/wiki/List_of_best-selling_music_artists?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="List
of
best-selling
music
artists">world's
best-selling
artists
of
all
time</a>
having
sold
more
than
150
million
albums.<sup
id="cite_ref-5"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-5"><span>[</span>5<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>Brooks
has
released
six
albums
that
achieved
<a
href="/wiki/RIAA_certification?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="RIAA
certification">diamond</a>
status
in
the
United
States,
those
being:
<i><a
href="/wiki/Garth_Brooks_(album)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Garth
Brooks
(album)">Garth
Brooks</a></i>
(10&times;
platinum),
<i><a
href="/wiki/No_Fences?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="No
Fences">No
Fences</a></i>
(17&times;
platinum),
<i><a
href="/wiki/Ropin%27_the_Wind?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Ropin'
the
Wind">Ropin'
the
Wind</a></i>
(14&times;
platinum),
<i><a
href="/wiki/The_Hits_(Garth_Brooks_album)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="The
Hits
(Garth
Brooks
album)">The
Hits</a></i>
(10&times;
platinum),
<i><a
href="/wiki/Sevens_(album)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Sevens
(album)">Sevens</a></i>
(10&times;
platinum)
and
<i><a
href="/wiki/Double_Live_(Garth_Brooks_album)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Double
Live
(Garth
Brooks
album)">Double
Live</a></i>
(21&times;
platinum).<sup
id="cite_ref-GarthBrooksASearch_6-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-GarthBrooksASearch-6"><span>[</span>6<span>]</span></a></sup>
Since
1989,
Brooks
has
released
19
records
in
all,
which
include;
10
studio
albums,
1
live
album,
3
compilation
albums,
3
Christmas
albums
and
3
box
sets,
along
with
77
singles.
He
won
several
important
awards
in
his
career,
including
2
<a
href="/wiki/Grammy_Awards?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Grammy
Awards"
class="mw-redirect">Grammy
Awards</a>,
17
<a
href="/wiki/American_Music_Awards?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="American
Music
Awards"
class="mw-redirect">American
Music
Awards</a>
(including
the
&quot;Artist
of
the
'90s&quot;)
and
the
<a
href="/wiki/Recording_Industry_Association_of_America?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Recording
Industry
Association
of
America">RIAA
Award</a>
as
Best
selling
solo
albums
artist
of
the
Century
in
the
United
States.</p>








<p>Troubled
by
conflicts
between
career
and
family,
Brooks
officially
retired
from
recording
and
performing
from
2001
until
2009.<sup
id="cite_ref-johnsonag_1-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-johnsonag-1"><span>[</span>1<span>]</span></a></sup>
During
this
time,
he
sold
millions
of
albums
through
an
exclusive
distribution
deal
with
<a
href="/wiki/Walmart?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Walmart">Walmart</a>
and
sporadically
released
new
singles.<sup
id="cite_ref-boxset_7-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-boxset-7"><span>[</span>7<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-ledoux_8-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-ledoux-8"><span>[</span>8<span>]</span></a></sup>
In
2005,
Brooks
started
a
partial
comeback,
and
has
since
given
several
performances
and
released
two
compilation
albums.</p>








<p>On
October
15,
2009,
Garth
Brooks
announced
the
end
of
his
retirement.
In
December
2009,
he
began
a
five-year
concert
deal
with
the
<a
href="/wiki/Encore_Las_Vegas?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Encore
Las
Vegas">Encore
Hotel
and
Casino</a>
on
the
<a
href="/wiki/Las_Vegas_Strip?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Las
Vegas
Strip">Las
Vegas
Strip</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-9"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-9"><span>[</span>9<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>Brooks
was
inducted
into
the
<a
href="/wiki/Country_Music_Hall_of_Fame?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Country
Music
Hall
of
Fame"
class="mw-redirect">Country
Music
Hall
of
Fame</a>
on
October
21,
2012.<sup
id="cite_ref-10"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-10"><span>[</span>10<span>]</span></a></sup></p>

<tr

<h2><span
class="mw-headline"
id="Early_life_and_education">Early
life
and
education</span>
<span
class="mw-editsection">[<a
href="/wiki?title=Garth_Brooks&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1"
title="Edit
section:
Early
life
and
education">edit</a>]</span></h2>








<p>Troyal
Garth
Brooks
was
born
February
7,
1962,
in
<a
href="/wiki/Tulsa,_Oklahoma?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Tulsa,
Oklahoma">Tulsa,
Oklahoma</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-oklahistorical_11-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-oklahistorical-11"><span>[</span>11<span>]</span></a></sup>
He
was
the
youngest
child
of
Troyal
Raymond
Brooks,Jr
1931–2010,
a
<a
href="/wiki/Technical_drawing?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Technical
drawing">draftsman</a>
for
an
oil
company,
and
Colleen
McElroy
Carroll,1929–1999
a
1950s-era
country
singer
who
recorded
on
the
<a
href="/wiki/Capitol_Records?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Capitol
Records">Capitol
Records</a>
label
and
appeared
on
<i><a
href="/wiki/Ozark_Jubilee?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Ozark
Jubilee">Ozark
Jubilee</a></i>.<sup
id="cite_ref-mcgraw_12-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-mcgraw-12"><span>[</span>12<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-pond_13-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-pond-13"><span>[</span>13<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-hilburn_14-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-hilburn-14"><span>[</span>14<span>]</span></a></sup>
This
was
the
second
marriage
for
each
of
his
parents,
giving
Garth
four
older
half-siblings
(Jim,
Jerry,
Mike,
and
Betsy).
The
couple
had
two
children
together,
Kelly
and
Garth.<sup
id="cite_ref-cox4_15-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-cox4-15"><span>[</span>15<span>]</span></a></sup>
At
their
home
in
<a
href="/wiki/Yukon,_Oklahoma?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Yukon,
Oklahoma">Yukon,
Oklahoma</a>,
the
family
hosted
weekly
talent
nights.
All
of
the
children
were
required
to
participate,
either
by
singing
or
doing
skits.<sup
id="cite_ref-cox8_16-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-cox8-16"><span>[</span>16<span>]</span></a></sup>
Brooks
learned
to
play
both
the
guitar
and
banjo.<sup
id="cite_ref-cox9_17-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-cox9-17"><span>[</span>17<span>]</span></a></sup>
Colleen
died
of
throat
cancer
on
Aug
6th
1999.</p>








<p>As
a
child,
Garth
often
sang
in
casual
family
settings
but
his
primary
focus
was
athletics.
In
high
school,
he
played
football
and
baseball
and
ran
track
and
field.
He
received
a
track
scholarship
to
<a
href="/wiki/Oklahoma_State_University%E2%80%93Stillwater?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Oklahoma
State
University–Stillwater">Oklahoma
State
University</a>
in
<a
href="/wiki/Stillwater,_Oklahoma?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Stillwater,
Oklahoma">Stillwater</a>,
where
he
competed
in
the
<a
href="/wiki/Javelin_throw?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Javelin
throw">javelin</a>
and
was
a
member
of
<a
href="/wiki/Alpha_Gamma_Rho?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Alpha
Gamma
Rho">Alpha
Gamma
Rho</a>
fraternity.<sup
id="cite_ref-hilburn_14-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-hilburn-14"><span>[</span>14<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-seattletimes_18-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-seattletimes-18"><span>[</span>18<span>]</span></a></sup>
Brooks
graduated
in
1984
with
a
degree
in
advertising.<sup
id="cite_ref-seattletimes_18-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-seattletimes-18"><span>[</span>18<span>]</span></a></sup>
His
roommate,
<a
href="/wiki/Ty_England?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Ty
England">Ty
England</a>,
later
played
guitar
in
his
road
band
until
going
solo
in
1995.<sup
id="cite_ref-19"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-19"><span>[</span>19<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>Later
that
year,
Brooks
began
his
professional
music
career,
singing
and
playing
guitar
in
Oklahoma
clubs
and
bars,
most
notably
the
Tumbleweed
in
Stillwater.<sup
id="cite_ref-hilburn_14-2"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-hilburn-14"><span>[</span>14<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-seattletimes_18-2"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-seattletimes-18"><span>[</span>18<span>]</span></a></sup>
Through
his
elder
siblings,
Brooks
was
exposed
to
a
wide
range
of
music.
Although
he
listened
to
some
<a
href="/wiki/Country_music?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Country
music">country
music</a>,
especially
that
of
<a
href="/wiki/George_Jones?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="George
Jones">George
Jones</a>,
Brooks
was
most
fond
of
rock
music,
citing
<a
href="/wiki/James_Taylor?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="James
Taylor">James
Taylor</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/Dan_Fogelberg?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Dan
Fogelberg">Dan
Fogelberg</a>,
and
<a
href="/wiki/Townes_Van_Zandt?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Townes
Van
Zandt">Townes
Van
Zandt</a>
as
major
influences.<sup
id="cite_ref-cox8_16-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-cox8-16"><span>[</span>16<span>]</span></a></sup>
After
hearing
<i><a
href="/wiki/Unwound_(song)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Unwound
(song)">Unwound</a></i>,
<a
href="/wiki/George_Strait?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="George
Strait">George
Strait</a>'s
debut
single,
in
1981,
Brooks
decided
that
he
was
more
interested
in
playing
country
music.<sup
id="cite_ref-cox8_16-2"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-cox8-16"><span>[</span>16<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>In
1985,
entertainment
attorney
Rod
Phelps
drove
from
Dallas
to
listen
to
Brooks.
Phelps
liked
what
he
heard
and
offered
to
produce
Garth's
first
demo.
With
Phelps's
encouragement,
including
a
list
of
Phelps'
contacts
in
Nashville
and
some
of
his
credit
cards,<sup
id="cite_ref-20"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-20"><span>[</span>20<span>]</span></a></sup>
Brooks
traveled
to
<a
href="/wiki/Nashville,_Tennessee?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Nashville,
Tennessee">Nashville</a>
to
pursue
a
recording
contract;
he
returned
to
Oklahoma
within
24
hours.
Phelps
continued
to
urge
Brooks
to
return
to
Nashville,
which
he
did.
In
1986,
Brooks
married
Sandy
Mahl,
whom
he
had
met
while
working
as
a
<a
href="/wiki/Bouncer_(doorman)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Bouncer
(doorman)">bouncer</a>.
In
1987,
the
couple
moved
to
Nashville,
and
Brooks
began
making
contacts
in
the
music
industry.
The
couple
later
had
three
daughters:
Taylor
Mayne
Pearl,
August
Anna,
and
Allie
Colleen.<sup
id="cite_ref-usgrandchild_21-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-usgrandchild-21"><span>[</span>21<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
couple
divorced
in
2000.<sup
id="cite_ref-usgrandchild_21-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-usgrandchild-21"><span>[</span>21<span>]</span></a></sup>
Garth
Brooks
remarried
on
December
10,
2005,
to
country
singer
<a
href="/wiki/Trisha_Yearwood?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Trisha
Yearwood">Trisha
Yearwood</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-hilburn_14-3"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-hilburn-14"><span>[</span>14<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-seattletimes_18-3"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-seattletimes-18"><span>[</span>18<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>Brooks
and
fellow
band
member
<a
href="/wiki/Jim_Garver?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Jim
Garver">Jim
Garver</a>
later
reminisced
of
their
times
traveling
with
small
shows
at
local
bars.
They
would
go
so
far
as
to
set
up
local
shows
under
the
stage
name
&quot;Yukon
Jack&quot;
to
re-live
those
days.<sup
id="cite_ref-22"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-22"><span>[</span>22<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<h2><span
class="mw-headline"
id="Career">Career</span>
<span
class="mw-editsection">[<a
href="/wiki?title=Garth_Brooks&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2"
title="Edit
section:
Career">edit</a>]</span></h2>








<h3><span
class="mw-headline"
id="1989.E2.80.931990:_Breakthrough_success">1989–1990:
Breakthrough
success</span>
<span
class="mw-editsection">[<a
href="/wiki?title=Garth_Brooks&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3"
title="Edit
section:
1989–1990:
Breakthrough
success">edit</a>]</span></h3>








<p>Garth
Brooks'
<a
href="/wiki/Garth_Brooks_(album)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Garth
Brooks
(album)">eponymous
first
album</a>
was
released
in
1989
and
was
a
critical
and
chart
success.
It
peaked
at
number
2
in
the
US
country
album
chart
and
reached
number
13
on
the
<a
href="/wiki/Billboard_200?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Billboard
200">Billboard
200</a>
pop
album
chart.
Most
of
the
album
was
traditionalist
country,
influenced
in
part
by
<a
href="/wiki/George_Strait?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="George
Strait">George
Strait</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-pond_13-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-pond-13"><span>[</span>13<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
first
single,
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Much_Too_Young_(To_Feel_This_Damn_Old)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Much
Too
Young
(To
Feel
This
Damn
Old)">Much
Too
Young
(To
Feel
This
Damn
Old)</a>&quot;,
was
a
country
top
10
success.
It
was
followed
by
his
first
country
number-one,
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/If_Tomorrow_Never_Comes?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="If
Tomorrow
Never
Comes">If
Tomorrow
Never
Comes</a>&quot;.
&quot;Not
Counting
You&quot;
reached
number
2,
and
then
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/The_Dance_(Garth_Brooks_song)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="The
Dance
(Garth
Brooks
song)"
class="mw-redirect">The
Dance</a>&quot;
put
him
at
number-one
again;
this
song's
theme
of
people
dying
while
doing
something
they
believe
in
resonated
strongly
and,
together
with
a
popular
music
video,
directed
by
<a
href="/wiki/John_Lloyd_Miller?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="John
Lloyd
Miller">John
Lloyd
Miller</a>,
gave
Brooks
his
first
push
towards
a
broader
audience.
Brooks
has
claimed
that
out
of
all
the
songs
he
has
recorded,
&quot;The
Dance&quot;
is
his
favorite.<sup
id="cite_ref-pond_13-2"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-pond-13"><span>[</span>13<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>His
follow-up
album,
<i><a
href="/wiki/No_Fences?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="No
Fences">No
Fences</a></i>,
was
released
in
1990
and
spent
23
weeks
as
number-one
on
the
Billboard
country
music
chart.<sup
id="cite_ref-erlewine_23-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-erlewine-23"><span>[</span>23<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
album
also
reached
number
3
on
the
pop
chart,
and
eventually
became
Brooks's
highest-selling
album,
with
domestic
shipments
of
17
million.<sup
id="cite_ref-riaa_24-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-riaa-24"><span>[</span>24<span>]</span></a></sup>
It
contained
what
would
become
Brooks's
<a
href="/wiki/Signature_song?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Signature
song">signature
song</a>,
the
<a
href="/wiki/Blue_collar?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Blue
collar"
class="mw-redirect">blue
collar</a>
anthem
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Friends_in_Low_Places?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Friends
in
Low
Places">Friends
in
Low
Places</a>&quot;,
as
well
as
two
other
Brooks
classics,
the
dramatic
and
controversial
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/The_Thunder_Rolls?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="The
Thunder
Rolls">The
Thunder
Rolls</a>&quot;
and
the
philosophically
ironic
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Unanswered_Prayers?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Unanswered
Prayers">Unanswered
Prayers</a>&quot;.</p>








<table
class="mbox-small"

#aaa;

of
Brooks's
song,














<a

colspan="2"
class="mbox-text"
style="line-height:1.1em;"><span
style="font-size:smaller;"><i>Problems
playing
this
file?

<a

target="_blank"
title="Wikipedia:Media
help">media
help</a>.</i></span></td>

</table>








<p>Each
of
these
songs,
as
well
as
the
affectionate
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Two_of_a_Kind,_Workin%27_on_a_Full_House?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Two
of
a
Kind,
Workin'
on
a
Full
House">Two
of
a
Kind,
Workin'
on
a
Full
House</a>&quot;,
reached
number-one
on
the
country
chart.<sup
id="cite_ref-pond_13-3"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-pond-13"><span>[</span>13<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-erlewine_23-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-erlewine-23"><span>[</span>23<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>While
Brooks's
musical
style
placed
him
squarely
within
the
boundaries
of
country
music,
he
was
strongly
influenced
by
the
1970s
singer-songwriter
movement,
especially
the
works
of
<a
href="/wiki/James_Taylor?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="James
Taylor">James
Taylor</a>
(whom
he
idolized
and
named
his
first
child
after)
and
<a
href="/wiki/Dan_Fogelberg?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Dan
Fogelberg">Dan
Fogelberg</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-hurst_25-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-hurst-25"><span>[</span>25<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-whitemojo_26-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-whitemojo-26"><span>[</span>26<span>]</span></a></sup>
Similarly,
Brooks
was
influenced
by
1970s-era
rock
of
<a
href="/wiki/Billy_Joel?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Billy
Joel">Billy
Joel</a>,
and
<a
href="/wiki/Bruce_Springsteen?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Bruce
Springsteen">Bruce
Springsteen</a>
and
the
operatic
rock
of
<a
href="/wiki/Queen_(band)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Queen
(band)">Queen</a>
with
<a
href="/wiki/Freddie_Mercury?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Freddie
Mercury">Freddie
Mercury</a>.
In
his
highly
successful
live
shows,
Brooks
used
a
wireless
headset
microphone
to
free
himself
to
run
about
the
stage,
adding
energy
and
<a
href="/wiki/Arena_rock?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Arena
rock">arena
rock</a>
theatrics
to
spice
up
the
normally
staid
country
music
approach
to
concerts.
The
hard
rock
band
<a
href="/wiki/KISS_(band)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="KISS
(band)"
class="mw-redirect">KISS</a>
was
also
one
of
his
earliest
grade
school
musical
influences
and
his
shows
often
reflected
this.
Brooks
said
that
the
style
of
his
show
was
inspired
mostly
by
<a
href="/wiki/Chris_LeDoux?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Chris
LeDoux">Chris
LeDoux</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-pareles_27-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-pareles-27"><span>[</span>27<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>Brooks
has
been
a
member
of
the
Grand
Ole
Opry
since
1990.<sup
id="cite_ref-28"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-28"><span>[</span>28<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-29"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-29"><span>[</span>29<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<h3><span
class="mw-headline"
id="1991.E2.80.9393:_Ropin.27_the_Wind_and_The_Chase">1991–93:
<i>Ropin'
the
Wind</i>
and
<i>The
Chase</i></span>
<span
class="mw-editsection">[<a
href="/wiki?title=Garth_Brooks&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4"
title="Edit
section:
1991–93:
Ropin'
the
Wind
and
The
Chase">edit</a>]</span></h3>








<p>Brooks's
third
album,
<i><a
href="/wiki/Ropin%27_the_Wind?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Ropin'
the
Wind">Ropin'
the
Wind</a></i>,
released
in
September
1991,
had
advance
orders
of
4
million
copies
and
entered
the
pop
album
charts
at
number-one,
a
first
for
a
country
act.<sup
id="cite_ref-mcgraw_12-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-mcgraw-12"><span>[</span>12<span>]</span></a></sup>
<i>Ropin'
the
Wind'</i>s
music
was
a
melange
of
pop
country
and
<a
href="/wiki/Honky_tonk_music?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Honky
tonk
music"
class="mw-redirect">honky
tonk</a>;
hits
included
Billy
Joel's
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Shameless_(song)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Shameless
(song)">Shameless</a>&quot;,
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/What_She%27s_Doing_Now?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="What
She's
Doing
Now">What
She's
Doing
Now</a>&quot;,
and
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/The_River_(Garth_Brooks_song)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="The
River
(Garth
Brooks
song)">The
River</a>&quot;.
All
told,
it
became
his
second-best
selling
album
after
<i>No
Fences</i>.
The
success
of
this
album
further
propelled
the
sales
of
his
first
two
albums,
enabling
Brooks
to
become
the
first
country
artist
with
three
albums
listed
in
the
pop
top
20
in
one
week.<sup
id="cite_ref-phillipsJan1992_30-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-phillipsJan1992-30"><span>[</span>30<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>After
spending
time
in
Los
Angeles
during
the
<a
href="/wiki/1992_Los_Angeles_riots?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="1992
Los
Angeles
riots">1992
riots</a>,
Brooks
co-wrote
the
gospel-country-rock
hybrid
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/We_Shall_Be_Free?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="We
Shall
Be
Free">We
Shall
Be
Free</a>&quot;
to
express
his
desire
for
tolerance.<sup
id="cite_ref-31"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-31"><span>[</span>31<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
song
became
the
first
single
off
his
fourth
album
<i><a
href="/wiki/The_Chase_(Garth_Brooks_album)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="The
Chase
(Garth
Brooks
album)">The
Chase</a></i>.
It
only
reached
number
12
on
the
country
chart,
his
first
song
in
three
years
to
fail
to
make
the
top
ten.<sup
id="cite_ref-latimes1993_32-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-latimes1993-32"><span>[</span>32<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-gray_33-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-gray-33"><span>[</span>33<span>]</span></a></sup>
Nevertheless,
the
song
often
received
<a
href="/wiki/Standing_ovation?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Standing
ovation">standing
ovations</a>
when
performed
in
concert,
went
to
number
22
in
the
Christian
charts
through
a
marketing
deal
with
Rick
Hendrix
Company,
and
earned
Brooks
a
1993
<a
href="/wiki/GLAAD_Media_Awards?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="GLAAD
Media
Awards"
class="mw-redirect">GLAAD
Media
Award</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-34"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-34"><span>[</span>34<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-phillips1992_35-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-phillips1992-35"><span>[</span>35<span>]</span></a></sup>
Following
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/We_Shall_Be_Free?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="We
Shall
Be
Free">We
Shall
Be
Free</a>&quot;,
the
next
single
released
in
would
be
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Somewhere_Other_Than_the_Night?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Somewhere
Other
Than
the
Night">Somewhere
Other
Than
the
Night</a>&quot;,
which
peaked
at
number
1
in
late
1992,
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Learning_to_Live_Again?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Learning
to
Live
Again">Learning
to
Live
Again</a>&quot;,
a
number
2
hit
in
1993.
The
final
single
off
of
<i>The
Chase</i>
would
be
1993's
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/That_Summer_(song)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="That
Summer
(song)">That
Summer</a>&quot;,
which
would
go
on
to
be
the
most
successful
single
from
the
album,
reaching
number
1
in
July
1993,
it
is
also
one
of
Brooks'
most
recognizable
songs.</p>








<h3><span
class="mw-headline"
id="1993.E2.80.9394:_In_Pieces">1993–94:
<i>In
Pieces</i></span>
<span
class="mw-editsection">[<a
href="/wiki?title=Garth_Brooks&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5"
title="Edit
section:
1993–94:
In
Pieces">edit</a>]</span></h3>








<p>In
1993,
Garth
Brooks,
who
had
criticized
music
stores
which
sold
used
CDs
since
it
led
to
a
loss
in
royalty
payments,
persuaded
Capitol
Records
not
to
ship
his
August
1993
album
<i>In
Pieces</i>
to
stores
which
engaged
in
this
practice.
This
led
to
several
<a
href="/wiki/Anti-trust?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Anti-trust"
class="mw-redirect">anti-trust</a>
lawsuits
against
the
record
label
and
ended
with
Capitol
shipping
the
CDs
to
the
stores
after
all.<sup
id="cite_ref-philips_36-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-philips-36"><span>[</span>36<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>Despite
the
delay
in
shipping
the
album
to
certain
stores,
<i><a
href="/wiki/In_Pieces?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="In
Pieces">In
Pieces</a></i>
was
another
instant
No.
1
success,
selling
a
total
of
about
10
million
copies
worldwide.
Some
of
his
fans
were
upset,
however,
that
the
album
was
not
released
simultaneously
around
the
world.
In
the
United
Kingdom,
one
of
Brooks's
most
committed
fan
bases
outside
the
United
States,
country
music
disc
jockeys,
such
as
Martin
Campbell
and
John
Wellington,
noted
that
many
fans
were
buying
the
album
on
import.
This
made
it
the
first
album
to
debut
in
the
top
10
of
the
UK
Country
album
charts
before
its
official
release
date.
Once
officially
released
there,
in
1994,
the
album
reached
the
top
spot
on
the
UK
Country
chart
-albeit
a
particularly
niche
chart
where
few
sales
are
needed
to
make
the
top
slots
–
and
number
two
on
the
UK
pop
albums
chart.
That
same
year
&quot;The
Red
Strokes&quot;
became
Brooks's
first
single
to
make
the
pop
top
40
in
the
UK,
reaching
a
high
of
No.
13;
it
was
followed
by
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Standing_Outside_The_Fire?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Standing
Outside
The
Fire"
class="mw-redirect">Standing
Outside
The
Fire</a>&quot;,
which
reached
No.
23.
Previous
albums
<i>No
Fences</i>,
<i>Ropin'
The
Wind</i>
and
<i>The
Chase</i>
also
remained
in
the
top
30
in
the
UK.</p>








<p>To
support
the
album,
Brooks
embarked
on
a
1994
UK
tour,
selling
out
venues
such
as
<a
href="/wiki/Birmingham?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Birmingham">Birmingham</a>'s
<a
href="/wiki/National_Exhibition_Centre?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="National
Exhibition
Centre">National
Exhibition
Centre</a>
and
London's
<a
href="/wiki/Wembley_Arena?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Wembley
Arena">Wembley
Arena</a>.
He
opened
the
London
radio
station,
<a
href="/wiki/Country_1035?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Country
1035">Country
1035</a>
and
made
a
number
of
general
television
and
radio
appearances,
where
he
was
often
mocked
by
the
presenters.
On
<a
href="/wiki/ITV_(TV_network)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="ITV
(TV
network)">ITV</a>'s
regional
news
show
<i><a
href="/wiki/London_Tonight?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="London
Tonight"
class="mw-redirect">London
Tonight</a></i>,
Brooks
was
described
as
&quot;a
top-selling,
rooting
tooting,
cotton
picking,
Country
and
Western
star,
yeeha!&quot;
The
nationwide
<i><a
href="/wiki/The_Big_Breakfast?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="The
Big
Breakfast">Big
Breakfast</a></i>
show's
presenters
<a
href="/wiki/Chris_Evans_(presenter)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Chris
Evans
(presenter)">Chris
Evans</a>
and
<a
href="/wiki/Paula_Yates?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Paula
Yates">Paula
Yates</a>,
commented
that
&quot;He's
selling
more
records
than
anyone
in
the
world,
but
none
of
us
have
ever
heard
of
him.&quot;
Yates
then
told
Brooks
that,
&quot;Country
singers
always
seem
to
be
weeping
over
the
dead
dog
and
things,&quot;
and
also
remarked,
&quot;I
thought
you'd
come
in
here
and
twiddle
your
pistol
around
and
be
impressed.&quot;
Although
Brooks
remained
polite,
he
did
observe
that
Yates
was
obviously
unfamiliar
with
modern
country
music.
Scores
of
Brooks
fans
later
wrote
to
complain
about
his
treatment
on
the
show.
Sometime
after
this,
<a
href="/wiki/Dwight_Yoakam?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Dwight
Yoakam">Dwight
Yoakam</a>
appeared
on
the
same
show
and
after
Yates
told
him,
&quot;You
seem
different
from
other
country
singers
we've
had
on
the
show,&quot;
Yoakam
replied,
&quot;What?
All
two
of
us?&quot;</p>








<p>Despite
the
disdain
of
the
British
media,
Brooks's
overall
popularity
in
the
country
was
evident,
with
a
top
<a
href="/wiki/Disc_jockey?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Disc
jockey">disc
jockey</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/Nick_Barraclough?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Nick
Barraclough">Nick
Barraclough</a>,
referring
to
Brooks
as
Garth
Vader
(a
play
on
<a
href="/wiki/Darth_Vader?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Darth
Vader">Darth
Vader</a>)
for
his
&quot;invasion&quot;
of
the
charts
and
his
success
in
the
country
genre.
Unlike
<a
href="/wiki/Alan_Jackson?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Alan
Jackson">Alan
Jackson</a>,
who
refused
to
return
to
the
UK
after
being
treated
in
a
similar
manner
by
the
press,
Brooks
returned
in
1996
for
more
sold-out
concerts,
although
this
time
his
media
appearances
were
mostly
restricted
to
country
radio
and
interviews
with
<a
href="/wiki/Magazine?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Magazine">magazines</a>.</p>








<p>Elsewhere
in
the
world
Brooks
was
also
considered
a
star,
and
he
enjoyed
hit
records
and
sell-out
tours
in
regions
including
Brazil,
throughout
Europe,
the
<a
href="/wiki/Far_East?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Far
East">Far
East</a>,
New
Zealand,
and
Australia.<sup
id="cite_ref-sandler_37-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-sandler-37"><span>[</span>37<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>In
1994
Brooks
paid
homage
to
one
of
his
musical
influences
when
he
appeared
on
the
tribute
compilation
<i><a
href="/wiki/Kiss_My_Ass:_Classic_Kiss_Regrooved?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Kiss
My
Ass:
Classic
Kiss
Regrooved">Kiss
My
Ass:
Classic
Kiss
Regrooved</a>,</i>
a
collection
of
<a
href="/wiki/Kiss_(band)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Kiss
(band)">Kiss</a>
songs
performed
by
popular
artists
from
various
genres.
As
the
only
country
performer
to
participate,
some<sup
class="noprint
Inline-Template"
style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a
href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia:Avoid_weasel_words"
target="_blank"
title="Wikipedia:Avoid
weasel
words"><span
title="The
material
near
this
tag
possibly
uses
too-vague
attribution
or
weasel
words.
(January
2014)">who?</span></a></i>]</sup>
worried
that
Brooks
would
turn
his
cover
of
the
song
originally
sung
by
drummer
<a
href="/wiki/Peter_Criss?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Peter
Criss">Peter
Criss</a>,
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Hard_Luck_Woman?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Hard
Luck
Woman">Hard
Luck
Woman</a>&quot;,
into
a
country
song.
Brooks
instead
insisted
on
remaining
true
to
the
song,
and
requested
that
the
members
of
Kiss
perform
the
music
on
the
track,
making
it
the
only
song
on
the
album
to
bear
a
musical
contribution
from
<a
href="/wiki/Kiss_(band)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Kiss
(band)">Kiss</a>.
The
unlikely
collaboration
performed
the
song
live
on
<i><a
href="/wiki/The_Tonight_Show_with_Jay_Leno?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="The
Tonight
Show
with
Jay
Leno">The
Tonight
Show
with
Jay
Leno</a></i>
in
promotion
of
<i><a
href="/wiki/Kiss_My_Ass:_Classic_Kiss_Regrooved?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Kiss
My
Ass:
Classic
Kiss
Regrooved">Kiss
My
Ass:
Classic
Kiss
Regrooved</a>,</i>
and
despite
its
hard-rock
appeal,
Brooks's
version
did
appear
on
the
country
charts.</p>








<h3><span
class="mw-headline"
id="Pop_crossover_success">Pop
crossover
success</span>
<span
class="mw-editsection">[<a
href="/wiki?title=Garth_Brooks&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6"
title="Edit
section:
Pop
crossover
success">edit</a>]</span></h3>








<h3><span
class="mw-headline"
id="1995.E2.80.931998:_Success_in_the_mid-to-late_1990s">1995–1998:
Success
in
the
mid-to-late
1990s</span>
<span
class="mw-editsection">[<a
href="/wiki?title=Garth_Brooks&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7"
title="Edit
section:
1995–1998:
Success
in
the
mid-to-late
1990s">edit</a>]</span></h3>








<p>In
November
1995
Brooks
released
<i><a
href="/wiki/Fresh_Horses_(album)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Fresh
Horses
(album)">Fresh
Horses</a></i>,
his
first
album
of
new
material
in
two
years;
within
six
months
of
its
release,
it
had
sold
over
three
million
copies.
Despite
its
promising
start,
Fresh
Horses
plateaued
quickly,
topping
out
at
quadruple
platinum.<sup
id="cite_ref-allmusic_38-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-allmusic-38"><span>[</span>38<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
album's
lead
single,
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/She%27s_Every_Woman?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="She's
Every
Woman">She's
Every
Woman</a>&quot;
peaked
at
number-one
on
the
<a
href="/wiki/Hot_Country_Songs?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Hot
Country
Songs">Billboard
Country
Chart</a>,
however
its
follow-up
single,
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Fever_(Aerosmith_song)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Fever
(Aerosmith
song)">The
Fever</a>&quot;
(a
cover
of
an
Aerosmith
song
)
only
peaked
at
number
23,
becoming
Brooks's
first
released
Country
single
to
not
chart
on
the
Top
10.
However,
Brooks
had
three
additional
Top
10
hits
from
the
album
following
the
second
single,
including
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/The_Beaches_of_Cheyenne?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="The
Beaches
of
Cheyenne">The
Beaches
of
Cheyenne</a>&quot;,
that
also
hit
number
one.</p>








<p>In
1997,
Brooks
released
his
seventh
studio
album,
<i><a
href="/wiki/Sevens_(album)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Sevens
(album)">Sevens</a></i>.
Originally,
it
was
scheduled
to
be
released
in
August
1997,
when
he
would
promote
it
with
a
concert
in
<a
href="/wiki/Central_Park?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Central
Park">Central
Park</a>.
Plans
went
awry
when
Capitol
Records
experienced
a
huge
management
shakeup,
leaving
many
of
his
contacts
at
the
label
out
in
the
cold.<sup
id="cite_ref-allmusic_38-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-allmusic-38"><span>[</span>38<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
album
was
then
released
in
November
1997,
and
debuted
at
number-one
on
both
the
<a
href="/wiki/Top_Country_Albums?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Top
Country
Albums"
class="mw-redirect">Top
Country
Albums</a>
and
<a
href="/wiki/Billboard_200?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Billboard
200">Billboard
200</a>
album
charts
in
the
United
States,
and
later
became
his
fourth
album
to
reach
a
sales
of
10
million
copies.
Its
first
single
was
also
Brooks's
first
duet,
&quot;In
Another's
Eyes&quot;
with
friend
and
popular
country
singer,
<a
href="/wiki/Trisha_Yearwood?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Trisha
Yearwood">Trisha
Yearwood</a>.
The
song
peaked
at
number
2
on
the
Country
Charts.
The
album
spawned
three
additional
Top
10
Country
hits,
including
two
number-one
hits
between
1997
and
1998,
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Two_Pina_Coladas?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Two
Pina
Coladas"
class="mw-redirect">Two
Pina
Coladas</a>&quot;
and
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/To_Make_You_Feel_My_Love?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="To
Make
You
Feel
My
Love"
class="mw-redirect">To
Make
You
Feel
My
Love</a>&quot;,
which
also
was
a
Top
10
hit
on
the
<a
href="/wiki/Hot_Adult_Contemporary_Tracks?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Hot
Adult
Contemporary
Tracks"
class="mw-redirect">Hot
Adult
Contemporary
Tracks</a>
chart
and
was
released
on
the
soundtrack
to
the
movie
Hope
Floats.</p>








<p>1998
saw
the
release
of
the
first
installment
of
<a
href="/wiki/The_Limited_Series_(1998_album)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="The
Limited
Series
(1998
album)"><i>The
Limited
Series</i>
(1998
album)</a>,
a
six-disc
box
set
containing
reissues
of
the
first
six
studio
releases
in
the
Garth
Brooks
catalog.
Each
of
the
reissued
compact
discs
included
a
bonus
track
not
available
on
the
original
release.</p>








<p>Brooks's
first
live
album,
<i><a
href="/wiki/Double_Live_(Garth_Brooks_album)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Double
Live
(Garth
Brooks
album)">Double
Live</a></i>
was
also
released
in
1998.
Recorded
at
various
shows
over
the
course
of
his
1998
world
tour,
as
opposed
to
being
a
document
of
one
show,
the
album
contained
material
released
up
to
the
<i><a
href="/wiki/Fresh_Horses_(album)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Fresh
Horses
(album)">Fresh
Horses</a></i>
album,
as
well
as
new
material
not
previously
released
elsewhere,
&quot;Tearin'
It
Up
(And
Burnin'
It
Down)&quot;
and
&quot;Wild
As
The
Wind,&quot;
featuring
<a
href="/wiki/Trisha_Yearwood?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Trisha
Yearwood">Trisha
Yearwood</a>.</p>








<h3><span
class="mw-headline"
id="1999:_Chris_Gaines">1999:
Chris
Gaines</span>
<span
class="mw-editsection">[<a
href="/wiki?title=Garth_Brooks&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8"
title="Edit
section:
1999:
Chris
Gaines">edit</a>]</span></h3>








<div
class="rellink
relarticle
mainarticle">








Main
article:









<a
href="/wiki/Chris_Gaines?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Chris
Gaines">Chris
Gaines</a>







</div>








<p>In
1999
Brooks
and
his
production
company
Red
Strokes
Entertainment,
with
<a
href="/wiki/Paramount_Pictures?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Paramount
Pictures">Paramount
Pictures</a>,
began
to
develop
a
movie
in
which
Brooks
would
star.
<i>The
Lamb</i>
was
to
have
revolved
around
<a
href="/wiki/Chris_Gaines?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Chris
Gaines">Chris
Gaines</a>,
a
fictional
rock
singer
and
his
emotionally
conflicted
life
as
a
musician
in
the
public
eye.
To
create
buzz
for
the
project,
Brooks
took
on
the
identity
of
Gaines
in
the
October
1999
album
<i><a
href="/wiki/Garth_Brooks_in_..._The_Life_of_Chris_Gaines?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Garth
Brooks
in
...
The
Life
of
Chris
Gaines"
class="mw-redirect">Garth
Brooks
in
...
The
Life
of
Chris
Gaines</a></i>,
which
was
intended
as
a
'pre-soundtrack'
to
the
film.<sup
id="cite_ref-gainescnn_39-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-gainescnn-39"><span>[</span>39<span>]</span></a></sup>
Brooks
also
subsequently
appeared
as
Gaines
in
a
television
<a
href="/wiki/Mockumentary?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Mockumentary">mockumentary</a>
for
the
<a
href="/wiki/VH1?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="VH1">VH1</a>
series
<i><a
href="/wiki/Behind_the_Music?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Behind
the
Music">Behind
the
Music</a></i>
and
as
the
musical
guest
on
an
episode
of
<i><a
href="/wiki/Saturday_Night_Live?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Saturday
Night
Live">Saturday
Night
Live</a></i>
which
he
hosted
as
himself.</p>








<p>Brooks's
endless
promotion
of
the
album
and
the
film
did
not
seem
to
stir
much
excitement
and
the
failure
of
the
Chris
Gaines
experiment
became
fairly
evident
mere
weeks
after
the
album
was
released.
Although
critics
admired
Brooks
for
taking
a
musical
risk,
the
majority
of
the
American
public
was
either
totally
bewildered,
or
completely
unreceptive
to
the
idea
of
Garth
Brooks
as
anything
but
a
pop-country
singer.<sup
id="cite_ref-gaineserlewine_40-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-gaineserlewine-40"><span>[</span>40<span>]</span></a></sup>
Many
of
his
fans
also
felt
that
by
supporting
the
Gaines
project
they
would
lose
the
real
Garth
Brooks.<sup
id="cite_ref-gainesjohnson_41-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-gainesjohnson-41"><span>[</span>41<span>]</span></a></sup>
Sales
of
the
album
were
unspectacular
and
although
it
made
it
to
number
2
on
the
pop
album
chart,
expectations
had
been
higher
and
retail
stores
began
heavily
discounting
their
oversupply.<sup
id="cite_ref-gainesgoodman_42-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-gainesgoodman-42"><span>[</span>42<span>]</span></a></sup>
Less-than-expected
sales
of
the
album
(more
than
two
million)
and
no
further
developments
in
the
production
of
the
film
as
a
result
brought
the
project
to
an
indefinite
hiatus
in
February
2001
and
Gaines
quickly
faded
into
obscurity.<sup
id="cite_ref-lamb2003_43-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-lamb2003-43"><span>[</span>43<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>Despite
the
less-than-spectacular
response
to
the
Chris
Gaines
project,
Brooks
gained
his
first
–
and
only
–
US
Top
40
pop
single
in
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Lost_in_You_(Chris_Gaines_song)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Lost
in
You
(Chris
Gaines
song)">Lost
in
You</a>&quot;,
the
first
single
from
the
album.</p>








<h3><span
class="mw-headline"
id="2000.E2.80.932004:_Official_retirement">2000–2004:
Official
retirement</span>
<span
class="mw-editsection">[<a
href="/wiki?title=Garth_Brooks&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9"
title="Edit
section:
2000–2004:
Official
retirement">edit</a>]</span></h3>








<p>As
his
career
flourished,
Brooks
seemed
frustrated
by
the
conflicts
between
career
and
family.
He
talked
of
retiring
from
performing
in
1992<sup
id="cite_ref-latimes1993_32-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-latimes1993-32"><span>[</span>32<span>]</span></a></sup>
and
1995,
but
each
time
returned
to
touring.
In
1999
Brooks
appeared
on
<a
href="/wiki/The_Nashville_Network?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="The
Nashville
Network">The
Nashville
Network</a>'s
<i>Crook
&amp;
Chase</i>
program
and
again
mentioned
retirement.<sup
id="cite_ref-boehlert_44-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-boehlert-44"><span>[</span>44<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>On
October
26,
2000,
Brooks
officially
announced
his
retirement
from
recording
and
performing.<sup
id="cite_ref-rosen2_45-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-rosen2-45"><span>[</span>45<span>]</span></a></sup>
Later
that
evening,
Capitol
Records
saluted
his
achievement
of
selling
100
million
albums
in
the
US
with
a
lavish
party
at
Nashville's
<a
href="/wiki/Gaylord_Entertainment_Center?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Gaylord
Entertainment
Center"
class="mw-redirect">Gaylord
Entertainment
Center</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-rosen_46-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-rosen-46"><span>[</span>46<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>Brooks's
final
album,
<i><a
href="/wiki/Scarecrow_(Garth_Brooks_album)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Scarecrow
(Garth
Brooks
album)">Scarecrow</a></i>,
was
released
on
November
13,
2001.
The
album
did
not
match
the
sales
levels
of
Brooks's
heyday,
but
still
sold
comfortably
well,
reaching
number-one
on
both
the
pop
and
country
charts.
Although
he
staged
a
few
performances
for
promotional
purposes,
Brooks
stated
that
he
would
be
retired
from
recording
and
performing
at
least
until
his
youngest
daughter,
Allie,
turned
18.
Despite
ceasing
to
record
new
material
between
2002
and
(most
of)
2005,
Brooks
continued
to
chart
with
previously
recorded
material,
including
a
top
30
placing
for
&quot;Why
Ain't
I
Running&quot;
in
2003.</p>








<h3><span
class="mw-headline"
id="2005.E2.80.932008">2005–2008</span>
<span
class="mw-editsection">[<a
href="/wiki?title=Garth_Brooks&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10"
title="Edit
section:
2005–2008">edit</a>]</span></h3>








<p>In
2005,
Brooks
insisted
that
he
was
not
touring
and
did
not
plan
to
record
any
new
studio
material
until
at
least
2015.
However,
in
August
2005
it
was
announced
that
Brooks
had
signed
a
deal
with
<a
href="/wiki/Wal-Mart?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Wal-Mart"
class="mw-redirect">Wal-Mart</a>,
leasing
them
the
rights
to
his
back
catalog
following
his
split
with
Capitol.<sup
id="cite_ref-newman_47-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-newman-47"><span>[</span>47<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-leavelabel_48-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-leavelabel-48"><span>[</span>48<span>]</span></a></sup>
Three
months
later,
Brooks
and
Wal-Mart
issued
<i><a
href="/wiki/The_Limited_Series_(2005_box_set)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="The
Limited
Series
(2005
box
set)"
class="mw-redirect">The
Limited
Series</a></i>,
a
six-CD
box
set
containing
re-issues
of
Garth's
full
length
albums
released
subsequent
to
<i><a
href="/wiki/Fresh_Horses_(album)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Fresh
Horses
(album)">Fresh
Horses</a></i>,
including
<i><a
href="/wiki/Double_Live_(Garth_Brooks_album)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Double
Live
(Garth
Brooks
album)">Double
Live</a></i>
and
a
<i>Lost
Sessions</i>
disc
with
eleven
previously
unreleased
recordings.
This
set
marked
the
first
time
in
history
that
a
musician
had
signed
an
exclusive
music
distribution
deal
with
a
single
retailer.<sup
id="cite_ref-newman_47-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-newman-47"><span>[</span>47<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
set
sold
more
than
500,000
physical
copies
on
its
issue
date,
proving
that
Brooks
still
had
a
large
fan
base.
By
the
first
week
in
December
2005,
it
had
sold
over
1
million
physical
copies.<sup
id="cite_ref-boxset_7-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-boxset-7"><span>[</span>7<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>Brooks
took
a
brief
break
from
retirement
early
in
2005
to
perform
for
several
charity
causes.
With
Yearwood,
he
sang
<a
href="/wiki/Creedence_Clearwater_Revival?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Creedence
Clearwater
Revival">Creedence
Clearwater
Revival</a>'s
&quot;Who'll
Stop
the
Rain&quot;
on
the
<i><a
href="/wiki/Shelter_from_the_Storm:_A_Concert_for_the_Gulf_Coast?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Shelter
from
the
Storm:
A
Concert
for
the
Gulf
Coast">Shelter
from
the
Storm:
A
Concert
for
the
Gulf
Coast</a></i>
nationwide
telethon
for
<a
href="/wiki/Hurricane_Katrina?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Hurricane
Katrina">Hurricane
Katrina</a>
relief.<sup
id="cite_ref-shelter_49-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-shelter-49"><span>[</span>49<span>]</span></a></sup>
He
also
released
a
new
single,
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Good_Ride_Cowboy?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Good
Ride
Cowboy">Good
Ride
Cowboy</a>&quot;,
as
a
tribute
to
his
late
friend,
rodeo
star
and
country
singer,
<a
href="/wiki/Chris_LeDoux?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Chris
LeDoux">Chris
LeDoux</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-ledoux_8-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-ledoux-8"><span>[</span>8<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>In
early
2006
Wal-Mart
re-issued
<i>The
Lost
Sessions</i>
as
a
single
CD
apart
from
the
boxed
set,
with
extra
tracks
including
a
top
25
duet
with
Yearwood,
&quot;Love
Will
Always
Win&quot;.<sup
id="cite_ref-lostsessions_50-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-lostsessions-50"><span>[</span>50<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
couple
were
later
nominated
for
a
&quot;Best
Country
Collaboration
With
Vocals&quot;
Grammy
Award
for
the
song.</p>








<p>On
August
18,
2007,
Brooks
announced
plans
for
a
new
boxed
set
called
<i><a
href="/wiki/The_Ultimate_Hits?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="The
Ultimate
Hits">The
Ultimate
Hits</a></i>.
The
new
set
features
two
discs
containing
30
hits,
three
new
songs,
and
a
DVD
featuring
music
videos
for
each
of
these
songs.
The
album's
first
single,
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/More_Than_a_Memory?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="More
Than
a
Memory">More
Than
a
Memory</a>&quot;,
was
released
to
radio
on
August
27,
2007.<sup
id="cite_ref-51"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-51"><span>[</span>51<span>]</span></a></sup>
&quot;More
Than
a
Memory&quot;
debuted
at
number
one
on
the
<i>Billboard</i>
<a
href="/wiki/Hot_Country_Songs?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Hot
Country
Songs">Hot
Country
Songs</a>
chart,
becoming
the
highest-debuting
single
in
the
chart's
history.
The
previous
record
had
been
set
only
one
week
earlier,
when
<a
href="/wiki/Kenny_Chesney?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Kenny
Chesney">Kenny
Chesney</a>'s
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Don%27t_Blink?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Don't
Blink">Don't
Blink</a>&quot;
debuted
at
number
16.<sup
id="cite_ref-52"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-52"><span>[</span>52<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>In
November
2007,
Brooks
performed
nine
sold-out
shows
in
Kansas
City
at
the
<a
href="/wiki/Sprint_Center?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Sprint
Center">Sprint
Center</a>,
which
had
opened
a
month
prior.
Originally
scheduled
to
be
only
one
show,
the
performance
expanded
to
nine
due
to
incredibly
high
demand,
with
all
nine
shows
(equaling
about
140,000
tickets)
selling
out
in
under
two
hours.<sup
id="cite_ref-53"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-53"><span>[</span>53<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
shows
took
place
from
November
5
to
November
12,
with
the
final
show
on
November
14
–
the
final
show
was
simulcast
to
more
than
300
movie
theaters
across
the
U.S.<sup
id="cite_ref-54"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-54"><span>[</span>54<span>]</span></a></sup></p>

Brooks
at
the











<a

onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"

The

at
the

Memorial">We
Are
One</a>
concert
in
2009









</div>









</div>








</div>








<p>Brooks
performed
five
sold
out
concerts
over
two
days
at
the
Staples
Center
in
Los
Angeles,
California
on
January
25
and
26,
2008
(setting
numerous
records
at
the
high
profile
venue
in
the
process).
These
concerts
were
staged
to
raise
money
for
firefighting
efforts
in
California
which
had
recently
been
ravaged
by
several
wildfires.
Tickets
were
priced
at
$40
each
and
all
five
shows
(totaling
more
than
85,000
tickets)
sold
out
in
58
minutes.
CBS
broadcast
the
first
concert
live
as
a
telethon
for
additional
fundraising.<sup
id="cite_ref-55"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-55"><span>[</span>55<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<h3><span
class="mw-headline"
id="2009.E2.80.93present:_return_to_performing">2009–present:
return
to
performing</span>
<span
class="mw-editsection">[<a
href="/wiki?title=Garth_Brooks&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11"
title="Edit
section:
2009–present:
return
to
performing">edit</a>]</span></h3>








<p>On
October
15,
2009,
Brooks
announced
that
he
was
coming
out
of
retirement
to
do
weekend
performances
at
Encore
Las
Vegas
on
the
Las
Vegas
Strip.
This
arrangement
continued
into
late
2012.
This
schedule
allowed
Brooks
both
to
have
the
family
life
for
which
he
had
retired
during
the
week
and
to
continue
to
perform
on
the
weekend.
On
October
28,
2010,
Garth
announced
he
would
do
his
first
&quot;arena&quot;
concert
in
Nashville
since
1998.
All
proceeds
benefits
the
Community
Foundation
in
Middle
Tennessee
in
support
of
all
those
Tennessee
residents
affected
by
the
disastrous
flooding
that
occurred
the
weekend
of
May
2,
2010.</p>








<p>The
financial
terms
of
the
agreement
have
not
been
announced,
but
Wynn
did
disclose
that
he
gave
Brooks
access
to
a
private
jet
to
quickly
transport
him
between
<a
href="/wiki/Las_Vegas_Valley?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Las
Vegas
Valley">Las
Vegas</a>
and
his
home
in
<a
href="/wiki/Oklahoma?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Oklahoma">Oklahoma</a>.</p>








<p>Brooks's
first
weekend
on
shows
in
Vegas
received
positive
reviews
and
was
called
the
&quot;antithesis
of
Vegas
glitz
and
of
the
country
singer's
arena
and
stadium
extravaganzas&quot;
by
USA
Today.
The
shows
feature
Brooks
performing
solo
with
his
own
guitar
accompaniment,
and
include
his
own
hits
as
well
as
songs
that
have
influenced
him.
Artists
covered
in
the
show
include
<a
href="/wiki/Simon_and_Garfunkel?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Simon
and
Garfunkel"
class="mw-redirect">Simon
and
Garfunkel</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/Bob_Seger?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Bob
Seger">Bob
Seger</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/Billy_Joel?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Billy
Joel">Billy
Joel</a>,
and
<a
href="/wiki/Don_McLean?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Don
McLean">Don
McLean</a>.
His
first
performances
at
Encore
Las
Vegas
coincided
with
his
wedding
anniversary,
and
his
wife
<a
href="/wiki/Trisha_Yearwood?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Trisha
Yearwood">Trisha
Yearwood</a>
joined
him
for
two
songs.</p>








<p>During
a
performance
on
August
19,
2011,
Brooks
told
his
audience
that
once
his
youngest
daughter
is
in
college
he
will
be
&quot;firing
the
tour
back
up.&quot;</p>








<p>On
July
12,
2012,
for
one
night
only,
Brooks
performed
in
front
of
a
sold
out
audience
at
<a
href="/wiki/Scotiabank_Saddledome?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Scotiabank
Saddledome">Scotiabank
Saddledome</a>
to
help
the
<a
href="/wiki/Calgary_Stampede?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Calgary
Stampede">Calgary
Stampede</a>
celebrate
its
centennial
anniversary.<sup
id="cite_ref-56"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-56"><span>[</span>56<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>In
October
2012,
it
was
noted
that
Brooks
was
nearing
the
end
of
his
residency
at
the
Wynn
in
Las
Vegas.
During
an
interview,
he
mentioned
that
he
would
still
do
'one-offs'
and
would
like
to
record
the
show
for
possible
DVD
release.
When
asked
about
a
comeback
in
2014,
he
said,
&quot;We'll
see..you
know
what's
in
my
heart
and
what
I
wanna
do,
but
we
just
can't
say
anything.&quot;<sup
id="cite_ref-57"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-57"><span>[</span>57<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>In
April
2013,
Brooks
and
George
Strait
performed
together
at
the
48th
annual
ACMAs
in
a
tribute
to
former
ACMA
producer
Dick
Clark,
in
the
first
such
performance
by
two
ACMA
Artists
of
the
Decade.<sup
id="cite_ref-58"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-58"><span>[</span>58<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>On
July
6,
2013,
Garth
Brooks
joined
with
<a
href="/wiki/Toby_Keith?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Toby
Keith">Toby
Keith</a>
to
put
on
a
benefit
concert
for
victims
of
the
2013
Oklahoma
tornadoes.
The
sold
out
concert
featured
artists
<a
href="/wiki/Mel_Tillis?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Mel
Tillis">Mel
Tillis</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/John_Anderson_(musician)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="John
Anderson
(musician)">John
Anderson</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/Willie_Nelson?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Willie
Nelson">Willie
Nelson</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/Trisha_Yearwood?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Trisha
Yearwood">Trisha
Yearwood</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/Sammy_Hagar?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Sammy
Hagar">Sammy
Hagar</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/Kellie_Coffey?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Kellie
Coffey">Kellie
Coffey</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/Ronnie_Dunn?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Ronnie
Dunn">Ronnie
Dunn</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/Carrie_Underwood?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Carrie
Underwood">Carrie
Underwood</a>
and
<a
href="/wiki/Krystal_Keith?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Krystal
Keith">Krystal
Keith</a>.
It
was
held
at
<a
href="/wiki/Gaylord_Family_Oklahoma_Memorial_Stadium?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Gaylord
Family
Oklahoma
Memorial
Stadium">Gaylord
Family
Oklahoma
Memorial
Stadium</a>
and
all
tickets
were
only
$25.
Brooks
told
Tulsa
World,
&quot;Once
we
got
the
news
that
the
tornado
had
hit
Toby's
hometown,
Miss
Yearwood
and
I
told
Toby
we
were
at
his
service
for
whatever
he
chose
to
do&nbsp;...
I
am
amazed
at
the
human
spirit
the
tornado
victims
have
shown.
I
am
humbled
by
the
giving
of
the
volunteers.
It
is
an
honor
to
get
to
be
a
part
of
this
healing
process.&quot;
This
was
the
first
time
Brooks
performed
in
his
home
state
of
Oklahoma
since
his
tour
in
1997.<sup
id="cite_ref-59"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-59"><span>[</span>59<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>In
December
2013,
Brooks
announced
he
and
his
band
are
going
on
a
world
tour
in
2014.<sup
id="cite_ref-gmatour_60-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-gmatour-60"><span>[</span>60<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>On
February
6,
2014,
Brooks
performed
<a
href="/wiki/The_Dance_(Garth_Brooks_song)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="The
Dance
(Garth
Brooks
song)"
class="mw-redirect">The
Dance</a>
on
the
final
episode
of
<a
href="/wiki/The_Tonight_Show_with_Jay_Leno?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="The
Tonight
Show
with
Jay
Leno">The
Tonight
Show
with
Jay
Leno</a>
and
later
closed
the
show
with
a
performance
of
<a
href="/wiki/Friends_in_Low_Places?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Friends
in
Low
Places">Friends
in
Low
Places</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-61"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-61"><span>[</span>61<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<h3><span
class="mw-headline"
id="Special_Ireland_Shows_2014">Special
Ireland
Shows
2014</span>
<span
class="mw-editsection">[<a
href="/wiki?title=Garth_Brooks&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12"
title="Edit
section:
Special
Ireland
Shows
2014">edit</a>]</span></h3>








<p>To
kickoff
his
new
tour
Brooks
announced
2
dates
at
<a
href="/wiki/Croke_Park?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Croke
Park">Croke
Park</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/Dublin?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Dublin">Dublin</a>,
Ireland
for
the
25th
and
26th
July
2014.
After
going
on
sale
the
tickets
sold
out
in
20
minutes.
A
third
date
was
soon
added
for
the
27th
of
July
but
this
sold
out
in
15
minutes.
There
was
anger
among
fans
as
some
people
were
purchasing
tickets
to
profit
by
reselling
at
higher
prices
(nearly
3
times
face
value).
A
few
days
after
saying
that
there
would
be
no
extra
shows
added,
Brooks
announced
a
4th
date
for
the
28th
of
July.
Tickets
for
this
date
went
on
sale
February
6th
at
9am
and
sold
out
in
just
25
minutes
after
going
on
sale.
After
selling
out
the
4th
date
Brooks
unexpectedly
announced
he
would
play
a
5th
date
and
tickets
for
this
show
sold
out
in
about
50
minutes.
In
total
400,000
tickets
were
sold
for
about
€28,600,000.
He
will
become
the
first
person
to
play
5
sold
out
shows
at
Croke
Park.</p>








<h2><span
class="mw-headline"
id="Personal_life">Personal
life</span>
<span
class="mw-editsection">[<a
href="/wiki?title=Garth_Brooks&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13"
title="Edit
section:
Personal
life">edit</a>]</span></h2>








<p>Brooks
graduated
from
<a
href="/wiki/Oklahoma_State_University?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Oklahoma
State
University"
class="mw-redirect">Oklahoma
State
University</a>
in
<a
href="/wiki/Stillwater,_Oklahoma?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Stillwater,
Oklahoma">Stillwater</a>,
as
a
brother
of
<a
href="/wiki/Alpha_Gamma_Rho?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Alpha
Gamma
Rho">Alpha
Gamma
Rho</a>
Fraternity,
where
he
starred
on
the
track
team.
He
later
completed
his
<a
href="/wiki/Master_of_Business_Administration?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Master
of
Business
Administration">MBA</a>
from
Oklahoma
State
and
participated
in
the
commencement
ceremony
on
May
6,
2011.<sup
id="cite_ref-62"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-62"><span>[</span>62<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<div
class="thumb
tright">

<a

/></a>

<div

</div>
Brooks'
second
wife
Trisha
Yearwood









</div>
