</div>








<p>Brooks
married
his
college
sweetheart,
songwriter
Sandy
Mahl,
on
May
24,
1986.
They
met
when
Garth
was
a
bouncer
at
a
bar.
Brooks
and
Mahl
separated
in
March
1999,
announcing
their
plans
to
divorce
on
October
9,
2000,
and
filing
for
divorce
on
November
6,
2000.<sup
id="cite_ref-rosen_46-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-rosen-46"><span>[</span>46<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-bbcnewsdivorce_63-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-bbcnewsdivorce-63"><span>[</span>63<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
divorce
became
final
on
December
17,
2001.<sup
id="cite_ref-bbcnewsdivorce_63-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-bbcnewsdivorce-63"><span>[</span>63<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-yearwoodaffair_64-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-yearwoodaffair-64"><span>[</span>64<span>]</span></a></sup>
Brooks
and
singer
<a
href="/wiki/Trisha_Yearwood?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Trisha
Yearwood">Trisha
Yearwood</a>
began
dating
after
Brooks's
divorce,
and
married
on
December
10,
2005,
at
their
home
in
Oklahoma,
marking
the
second
marriage
for
Brooks
and
the
third
for
Yearwood.
They
own
homes
in
<a
href="/wiki/Goodlettsville,_Tennessee?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Goodlettsville,
Tennessee">Goodlettsville,
Tennessee</a>;
<a
href="/wiki/Malibu,_California?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Malibu,
California">Malibu,
California</a>;
and
<a
href="/wiki/Port_St._Lucie,_Florida?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Port
St.
Lucie,
Florida">Port
St.
Lucie,
Florida</a>,
but
primarily
live
on
their
ranch
in
<a
href="/wiki/Owasso,_Oklahoma?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Owasso,
Oklahoma">Owasso,
Oklahoma</a>,
a
suburb
of
<a
href="/wiki/Tulsa,_Oklahoma?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Tulsa,
Oklahoma">Tulsa</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-65"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-65"><span>[</span>65<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>In
2000,
Brooks
attempted
to
donate
part
of
his
liver
to
country
music
contemporary,
and
close
friend,
<a
href="/wiki/Chris_LeDoux?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Chris
LeDoux">Chris
LeDoux</a>;
however,
it
was
found
to
be
incompatible.
LeDoux
received
another
donated
liver,
but
died
in
March
2005
due
to
complications
from
liver
cancer.<sup
id="cite_ref-66"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-66"><span>[</span>66<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<h2><span
class="mw-headline"
id="Professional_baseball">Professional
baseball</span>
<span
class="mw-editsection">[<a
href="/wiki?title=Garth_Brooks&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14"
title="Edit
section:
Professional
baseball">edit</a>]</span></h2>








<p>Brooks
set
out
on
a
short
and
unsuccessful
career
in
<a
href="/wiki/Baseball?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Baseball">baseball</a>,
when
he
signed
with
the
<a
href="/wiki/San_Diego_Padres?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="San
Diego
Padres">San
Diego
Padres</a>
for
<a
href="/wiki/Spring_training?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Spring
training">spring
training</a>
in
1998
<sup
id="cite_ref-67"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-67"><span>[</span>67<span>]</span></a></sup>
and
1999.<sup
id="cite_ref-68"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-68"><span>[</span>68<span>]</span></a></sup>
Some
in
the
media
mocked
the
decision
of
the
Padres
to
sign
a
country
music
star
in
his
late
thirties
whose
baseball
experience
ended
in
high
school.<sup
id="cite_ref-69"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-69"><span>[</span>69<span>]</span></a></sup>
Brooks'
performance
on
the
field
did
not
warrant
management
placing
him
on
the
regular
season
<a
href="/wiki/Roster?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Roster">roster</a>;
Brooks
was
offered
a
non-roster
spot
but
declined
it.<sup
id="cite_ref-70"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-70"><span>[</span>70<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>The
following
season,
Brooks
signed
with
the
<a
href="/wiki/New_York_Mets?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="New
York
Mets">New
York
Mets</a>.
This
time,
his
team
embraced
the
entertainment
value
of
having
a
<a
href="/wiki/Country_and_western?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Country
and
western"
class="mw-redirect">country
and
western</a>
star
on
the
<a
href="/wiki/Baseball_field?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Baseball
field">diamond</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-71"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-71"><span>[</span>71<span>]</span></a></sup>
This
spring-training
stint
was
also
a
poor
performance
for
Brooks,
however,
resulting
in
a
zero-for-seventeen
batting
record.<sup
id="cite_ref-72"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-72"><span>[</span>72<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>Brooks
returned
to
baseball,
one
last
time,
for
an
encore
performance
with
the
<a
href="/wiki/Kansas_City_Royals?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Kansas
City
Royals">Kansas
City
Royals</a>
in
2004.<sup
id="cite_ref-73"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-73"><span>[</span>73<span>]</span></a></sup>
In
baseball,
Brooks
never
matched
the
amount
of
hits
he
was
able
to
achieve
on
the
<a
href="/wiki/Music_charts?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Music
charts"
class="mw-redirect">music
charts</a>,
but
was
able
to
get
a
hit
off
<a
href="/wiki/Mike_Myers_(baseball)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Mike
Myers
(baseball)">Mike
Myers</a>
during
his
final
spring-training
season
with
the
Royals.<sup
class="Template-Fact"
style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a
href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed"
target="_blank"
title="Wikipedia:Citation
needed"><span
title="This
claim
needs
references
to
reliable
sources.
(January
2014)">citation
needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>








<h2><span
class="mw-headline"
id="Setting_records">Setting
records</span>
<span
class="mw-editsection">[<a
href="/wiki?title=Garth_Brooks&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15"
title="Edit
section:
Setting
records">edit</a>]</span></h2>








<p>The
<a
href="/wiki/Recording_Industry_Association_of_America?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Recording
Industry
Association
of
America">Recording
Industry
Association
of
America</a>
announced
that
Garth
Brooks
was
the
best-selling
solo
artist
of
the
20th
century
in
America.<sup
id="cite_ref-riaa1999_74-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-riaa1999-74"><span>[</span>74<span>]</span></a></sup>
This
conclusion
drew
criticism
from
the
press
and
many
music
fans
who
were
convinced
that
<a
href="/wiki/Elvis_Presley?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Elvis
Presley">Elvis
Presley</a>
had
sold
more
records,
but
had
been
short-changed
in
the
rankings
due
to
faulty
RIAA
certification
methods
during
his
lifetime.<sup
id="cite_ref-elvis1_75-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-elvis1-75"><span>[</span>75<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-quinn_76-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-quinn-76"><span>[</span>76<span>]</span></a></sup>
Brooks,
while
proud
of
his
sales
accomplishments,
stated
that
he
too
believed
that
Presley
must
have
sold
more.<sup
id="cite_ref-elvis1_75-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-elvis1-75"><span>[</span>75<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>The
RIAA
has
since
reexamined
their
methods
for
counting
certifications.
Under
their
revised
methods,
Presley
became
the
best-selling
solo
artist
in
U.S.
history,
making
Brooks
the
number
two
solo
artist,
ranking
third
overall,
as
<a
href="/wiki/The_Beatles?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="The
Beatles">The
Beatles</a>
have
sold
more
albums
than
either
he
or
Presley.<sup
id="cite_ref-riaatopartists_77-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-riaatopartists-77"><span>[</span>77<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
revision
brought
more
criticism
of
the
accuracy
of
the
RIAA's
figures,
this
time
from
Brooks's
followers.</p>








<p>On
November
5,
2007,
Brooks
was
again
named
the
best
selling
solo
artist
in
US
history,
surpassing
Presley
after
audited
sales
of
123
million
were
announced.<sup
id="cite_ref-78"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-78"><span>[</span>78<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>In
December
2010,
several
more
of
Presley's
albums
received
certifications
from
the
RIAA.
As
a
result,
Elvis
again
surpassed
Brooks.<sup
id="cite_ref-79"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-79"><span>[</span>79<span>]</span></a></sup>
As
of
June
2012,
the
RIAA
lists
Presley's
total
sales
at
134.5
million
and
Brooks's
at
128
million.<sup
id="cite_ref-80"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-80"><span>[</span>80<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>As
of
January
2012,
Brooks
officially
passed
the
Beatles
as
the
top-selling
act
of
the
past
20
years,
moving
68.5
million
units
worldwide,
almost
5
million
more
than
the
Beatles.<sup
id="cite_ref-81"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-81"><span>[</span>81<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<h2><span
class="mw-headline"
id="Charitable_activities">Charitable
activities</span>
<span
class="mw-editsection">[<a
href="/wiki?title=Garth_Brooks&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16"
title="Edit
section:
Charitable
activities">edit</a>]</span></h2>








<p>In
1999,
Garth
Brooks
began
the
<i>Teammates
for
Kids
Foundation</i><sup
id="cite_ref-teammatesforkids_82-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-teammatesforkids-82"><span>[</span>82<span>]</span></a></sup>
which
provides
financial
aid
to
charities
for
children.
The
organization
breaks
down
into
three
categories
spanning
three
different
sports:</p>








<ul>









<li>Touch
'Em
All
Foundation
–
Baseball
Division</li>









<li>Top
Shelf
–
Hockey
Division</li>









<li>Touchdown
–
Football
Division</li>








</ul>








<p>The
foundation
enlists
players
to
donate
a
predetermined
sum
of
money
depending
on
their
game
performance.
Brooks
has
participated
in
spring
training
for
the
<a
href="/wiki/San_Diego_Padres?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="San
Diego
Padres">San
Diego
Padres</a>
in
1998
and
1999,
the
<a
href="/wiki/New_York_Mets?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="New
York
Mets">New
York
Mets</a>
in
2000
and,
most
recently,
with
the
<a
href="/wiki/Kansas_City_Royals?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Kansas
City
Royals">Kansas
City
Royals</a>
in
2004
to
promote
his
foundation.
Starting
during
the
2008
season,
fans
at
Royals
games
in
<a
href="/wiki/Kauffman_Stadium?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Kauffman
Stadium">Kauffman
Stadium</a>
now
sing
along
to
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Friends_in_Low_Places?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Friends
in
Low
Places">Friends
in
Low
Places</a>&quot;.</p>








<p>Brooks
is
also
a
fundraiser
for
various
other
charities,
including
a
number
of
children's
charities
and
famine
relief.
He
has
also
donated
at
least
$1
million
to
wildlife
causes.
It
was
announced
that
Garth
would
perform
a
charity
concert
on
January
25
and
26,
2008,
at
the
<a
href="/wiki/Staples_Center?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Staples
Center">Staples
Center</a>
for
the
victims
of
the
recent
<a
href="/wiki/Category:Wildfires_in_California?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Category:Wildfires
in
California">California
Wildfires</a>.
On
December
1,
tickets
went
on
sale
and
sold
out
within
minutes,
prompting
them
to
announce
3
more
shows.
All
5
L.A.
shows
sold
out
in
less
than
59
minutes.
CBS
aired
the
first
of
these
concerts
(January
25
at
9
pm)
live,
giving
viewers
a
chance
to
donate
to
the
Firefighters
Relief
efforts.<sup
id="cite_ref-83"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-83"><span>[</span>83<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>In
December
2010,
Garth
played
9
shows
in
less
than
a
week
in
Nashville
at
<a
href="/wiki/Bridgestone_Arena?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Bridgestone
Arena">Bridgestone
Arena</a>
to
benefit
victims
from
the
<a
href="/wiki/2010_Tennessee_floods?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="2010
Tennessee
floods">May
2010
Nashville
flood</a>.
Over
140,000
tickets
were
sold
and
$5
million
raised.</p>








<p>A
$500,000
donation
Brooks
made
to
Integris
Canadian
Valley
Regional
Hospital
in
<a
href="/wiki/Yukon,_Oklahoma?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Yukon,
Oklahoma">Yukon,
Oklahoma</a>,
in
2005,
led
to
a
widely
publicized
lawsuit.
According
to
Brooks,
the
hospital
promised
to
name
a
new
women's
health
center
after
his
mother,
Colleen
Brooks,
who
died
of
cancer
in
1999;
the
hospital
later
decided
not
to
build
the
new
facility,
took
the
position
that
its
naming
commitment
was
non-binding,
and
refused
to
return
the
donation.
On
January
24,
2012,
an
Oklahoma
state
court
jury
in
<a
href="/wiki/Claremore,_Oklahoma?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Claremore,
Oklahoma">Claremore</a>
found
in
favor
of
Brooks,
ordering
the
hospital
to
pay
$500,000
for
the
original
donation
and
an
additional
$500,000
in
<a
href="/wiki/Punitive_damages?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Punitive
damages">punitive
damages</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-84"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-84"><span>[</span>84<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>Brooks,
along
with
<a
href="/wiki/Trisha_Yearwood?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Trisha
Yearwood">Trisha
Yearwood</a>,
has
supported
<a
href="/wiki/Habitat_for_Humanity?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Habitat
for
Humanity">Habitat
for
Humanity</a>'s
work
over
the
years,
including
the
annual
<a
href="/wiki/Jimmy_%26_Rosalynn_Carter_Work_Project?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Jimmy
&amp;
Rosalynn
Carter
Work
Project">Jimmy
&amp;
Rosalynn
Carter
Work
Project</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-85"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-85"><span>[</span>85<span>]</span></a></sup>
They
have
worked
alongside
the
Carters
in
the
United
States
and
in
Haiti,
lending
their
time
and
voices
to
help
build
safe,
decent
and
affordable
homes.
Brooks'
Teammates
for
Kids
Foundation
provided
more
than
$1
million
in
funding
to
Habitat
to
help
build
homes
in
Thailand
following
the
Asian
tsunami.<sup
id="cite_ref-86"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-86"><span>[</span>86<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<h3><span
class="mw-headline"
id="Support_for_gay_rights">Support
for
gay
rights</span>
<span
class="mw-editsection">[<a
href="/wiki?title=Garth_Brooks&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17"
title="Edit
section:
Support
for
gay
rights">edit</a>]</span></h3>








<p>In
the
lyrics
to
his
song
&quot;We
Shall
Be
Free&quot;,
Brooks
sings
&quot;When
we're
free
to
love
anyone
we
choose,&quot;
which
has
been
interpreted
as
a
reference
to
gay
relationships.<sup
id="cite_ref-George_87-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-George-87"><span>[</span>87<span>]</span></a></sup>
Brooks
won
a
1993
<a
href="/wiki/GLAAD_Media_Awards?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="GLAAD
Media
Awards"
class="mw-redirect">GLAAD
Media
Award</a>
for
the
song.
In
a
1999
interview
with
<i><a
href="/wiki/George_(magazine)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="George
(magazine)">George</a></i>,
Brooks
said,
&quot;[...]But
if
you're
in
love,
you've
got
to
follow
your
heart
and
trust
that
God
will
explain
to
us
why
we
sometimes
fall
in
love
with
people
of
the
same
sex.&quot;<sup
id="cite_ref-George_87-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-George-87"><span>[</span>87<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-GayToday_88-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-GayToday-88"><span>[</span>88<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>In
2000,
Brooks
appeared
at
the
<a
href="/wiki/Equality_Rocks?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Equality
Rocks"
class="mw-redirect">Equality
Rocks</a>
<a
href="/wiki/Benefit_concert?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Benefit
concert">benefit
concert</a>
for
<a
href="/wiki/Gay_rights?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Gay
rights"
class="mw-redirect">gay
rights</a>.
He
sang
a
duet
with
openly
gay
singer
<a
href="/wiki/George_Michael?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="George
Michael">George
Michael</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-CMTNews_89-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-CMTNews-89"><span>[</span>89<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>Brooks'
half-sister
Betsy
Smittle,
who
died
in
2013,
was
a
well-known
musician
and
part
of
Brooks'
band
for
some
years;
she
also
worked
with
the
late
country
star
<a
href="/wiki/Gus_Hardin?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Gus
Hardin">Gus
Hardin</a>
and
other
musicians
in
Tulsa.
Smittle
was
also
a
<a
href="/wiki/Lesbian?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Lesbian">lesbian</a>,
and
Brooks
has
credited
her
with
some
of
the
inspiration
for
his
tolerant
attitude.<sup
id="cite_ref-TulsaWorld_90-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-TulsaWorld-90"><span>[</span>90<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-OklahomaRock_91-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-OklahomaRock-91"><span>[</span>91<span>]</span></a></sup></p>

<script
type="text/javascript">




render_ads(false,
window['ad_config_bot']);





function
afc_match()
{








var
count
=
-1;








if(window['ad_config_top'])
{












count
=
window['ad_config_top'];








}









var
countBottom
=
0;








if(window['ad_config_bot'])
{












countBottom
=
window['ad_config_bot'];








}









if(window['backfillParam'])
{




























window['backfillParam']['pl_bmodn']
=
5;
























window['backfillParam']['pl_tnum']
=
count;












window['backfillParam']['pl_bnum']
=
countBottom;








}


































var
_matchUrl
=
"/afc-match?q=Garth_Brooks&page=1&ac=24&qid=D6FEAB2A64B9D25082E01C684933DBA3&qsrc=121&dm=&qrt=2&lid="+
"&o=0&l=dir&oo=&cl=ca-aj-cat&ch=cx_ask_wiki,ad_dirN";





















_matchUrl+=
"&userip=76.78.3.114";




































_matchUrl+="&losid=a&locid=encw&lodid=us&loaid=a16";









var
location
=
window.location
+
"";








location
=
location.substring(7);








var
cutIdx
=
location.indexOf("/");








if
(location.indexOf(":")
>
-1)
{




















cutIdx
=
1
+
cutIdx
+
location.substring(cutIdx+1).indexOf("/");








}









var
urlPrefix
=
location.substring(0,
cutIdx);








_matchUrl
=
"http://"
+
urlPrefix
+
_matchUrl
+
"&afcec="
+
count
+
"&afcecb="
+
countBottom;








ajax_get(_matchUrl,
null,
null);




}





function
getXHR()
{








if
(window.XMLHttpRequest)
{












return
new
XMLHttpRequest();








}
else
if
(window.ActiveXObject)
{












try
{
















return
new
ActiveXObject("Msxml2.XMLHTTP");












}
catch
(e)
{
















try
{




















return
new
ActiveXObject("Microsoft.XMLHTTP");
















}
catch
(E)
{




















return
null;
















}












}








}








else
{












return
null;








}




}





function
ajax_get(url,
onsuccess,
onerror)
{








var
obj
=
getXHR();








if(obj)
{












obj.onreadystatechange
=
function()
{
















if(obj.readyState==4)
{




















if
(obj.status
==
200
&&
typeof(onsuccess)
==
"function")
{
























onsuccess(obj);




















}
else
if
(typeof(onerror)
==
"function")
{
























onerror(obj);




















}






















try
{
























delete
obj['onreadystatechange'];




















}
catch(e)
{}
















}












};












obj.open("GET",
url,
true,
"",
"");












obj.send(null);












return
obj;








}
else
{












if(onerror)
{
















onerror("Error
creating
XHR");












}
else
{
















a10.debug("Error
creating
XHR");












}












return
null;








}




}





afc_match();

</script>
